B009MF56GC|2.0|\\"The Expendables 2\\" is only more of what you received with the first blockbuster film. It's definitely bigger with the introduction of new cast members such as Liam Hemsworth, Jean-Claude Van Damme, Scott Adkins, and Chuck Norris and bigger roles for Arnold Schwarzenegger and Bruce Willis, but is it better? How can a sequel and its predecessor bring together so many action stars and yet still leave so much to be desired? Somehow \\"The Expendables 2\\" tops the first movie in the sense that it leaves you with a craving for something a lot more satisfying.<br /><br />\\"The Expendables 2\\" was originally built around the death of Tool (Mickey Rourke) and Barney and his team getting revenge because of it. Well when Rourke suddenly pulled out for another project, that load was dumped onto Billy the Kid (Liam Hemsworth). The problem is you only get to know the character for approximately ten minutes before they pull the trigger. While Billy does manage to squeeze in a story about Afghanistan, another one about getting back to his girlfriend in France, and seems to have a father-son relationship with Barney, there isn't much of an impact since his character feels like the last minute replacement that it is.<br /><br />The writing isn't any better this time around. Sylvester Stallone is more than likely to blame as he should probably stick to acting and directing rather than chipping in with the screenplay. These guys say the most trivial and clich&eacute; one-liners you could possibly think of. \\"See you later, alligator,\\" and \\"Looks like somebody had a bad day,\\" are just a few examples. The motivations of several characters are really blurred, as well. Chuck Norris enters the picture as Booker, a sniper who claims that he only works alone and is a \\"lone wolf.\\" Then later shows up to help out Barney and his group again solely because, \\"Oh. Well, sometimes it's more fun to run with the pack.\\" The Church (Bruce Willis) character is the worst offender. He and Barney obviously have a history together, but in the first half of the movie he's rather villainous. He throws Barney and his team right into harm's way because Barney owes Church $5 million. Church threatens Barney and basically blackmails him into this mission. But then at the end of the movie, he helps Barney and they're good buddies by the final scene.<br /><br />Speaking of Church, his back and forth with Trench (Arnold Schwarzenegger) is also near unbearable. Schwarzenegger already made light of his \\"I'm back!\\" catchphrase in \\"Terminator 3,\\" so hearing him do it over and over again here is like beating a dead horse. Then Bruce Willis decides to say it and Arnold replies with, \\"Yippee ki yay,\\" before throwing in a \\"Rambo\\" reference a moment later. It just feels so elementary.<br /><br />Donnie Yen was originally offered a role in this film, but turned it down. So obviously Jet Li is going to pick up the slack, right? Nope, he bows out of the film after the first ten minutes. He does manage to throw in a pretty entertaining action sequence with frying pans before he leaves though. Scott Adkins is a martial arts actor who's finally managing to pick up steam. He's more than capable of putting on a good show, but doesn't get a chance to here. You also want to see more of Van Damme, but he's dealt with rather suddenly after only delivering two of his patented jumping roundhouse kicks. Speaking of Van Damme, his character's name is Vilain. How much thought was put into that?<br /><br />There are very few positives with \\"The Expendables 2.\\" Jason Statham has a few entertaining action sequences, but you're left wondering why one of those scenes couldn't have gone to somebody else. Dolph Lundgren's Gunnar character takes facts from his actual background like having a master's degree in engineering and even gets a bit more screen time. Aside from the opening sequence, which outdoes every explosive sequence in the first movie, explosions aren't as frequent this time around. Most of the actionlies within people's heads being blown off or fistfights that never seem to last as long as you want them to.<br /><br />\\"The Expendables 2\\" is only \\"bigger and better\\" in the sense that there are bigger additions to the cast, meatier roles for returning actors, and the amount of bullet casings collected when it's all said and done. But the downside is \\"The Expendables 2\\" is almost more of a letdown than the original movie. The dialogue is worse, character motivations are blurred, and the storyline is beyond simple. It's really only a great movie at face value because when you take a step back and realize how bad it is, you'll be left asking yourself how you gather this many well known stars in two movies and still manage to screw it up twice.<br /><br />In one of the special features, Sylvester Stallone talks about things being more grounded in \\"The Expendables 2.\\" He says that the first film was kind of all over the place in terms of character development and it was left up in the air on whether everyone was trying to be serious or slightly lighthearted at times. Stallone mentions that having that many big stars in one picture got to him the first time around and that it's better-rounded in the sequel. Maybe it is, but it still feels like Stallone is blinded by the dense fog that is made up of all these stars coming together. Everyone is just goofy as hell all the time and Barney and Christmas act like an old married couple. There's a difference in tapping into that same cheesiness that made up nearly every strand of DNA in action films of the 80s and 90s and overdoing it. \\"The Expendables 2\\" gets way too carried away with that aspect and dives into overkill territory more often than not.<br /><br />Special features on the Blu-ray edition of the film include Audio Commentary with director Simon West, the 21-minute \\"Gods of War: Assembling Earth's Mightiest Anti-Heroes,\\" the 25-minute \\"Big Guns, Bigger Heroes: The 1980s and the Rise of the Action Film,\\" the 14-minute \\"On the Assault: The Real-Life Weaponry of The Expendables 2,\\" the 24-minute \\"Guns For Hire: The Real Expendables,\\" four and a half minutes of deleted scenes, and a five-minute gag reel.ithin people's heads being blown off or fistfights that never seem to last as long as you want them to.<br /><br />\\"The Expendables 2\\" is only \\"bigger and better\\" in the sense that there are bigger additions to the cast, meatier roles for returning actors, and the amount of bullet casings collected when it's all said and done. B005LAIIHG|5.0|Ang Lee is a director that most individuals don't seem to be too fond of. To this day, his \\"Hulk\\" film remains unwatched because so many people have offered their opinion that it's awful. \\"Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon\\" is in the same category, but for different reasons. Wuxia films are almost always better when the wire work is more subtle and \\"Crouching Tiger\\" looks to take no shame in everyone flying around at all times. \\"Brokeback Mountain\\" was the only Lee film to be experienced before \\"Life of Pi\\" and that was solely because seeking out Heath Ledger's work seemed like a pretty vital thing to do after \\"The Dark Knight.\\" Going into \\"Life of Pi,\\" there was literally no interest. The book hadn't been read beforehand and trailers had not been seen. Expectations were mostly, \\"It may be gorgeous to look at, but will lack any sort of depth.\\" One of the best feelings in the world is having your misconceptions about something be completely wrong and work out in ways you never imagined.<br /><br />\\"Life of Pi\\" is narrated by an older Pi (Irrfan Khan) and takes place in the present as he tells his life story to a writer (Rafe Spall). Pi begins with how he got his name and how his family owned a zoo, but eventually leads into his family needing to leave India for financial purposes. The heart of the story lies in Pi as a young man (played by Suraj Sharma) and the time he spent out at sea on a lifeboat with a tiger named Richard Parker, but getting to that point is quite an ordeal. Pi loses everything and everyone close to him in the blink of an eye and he doesn't count on making what feels like an unbreakable bond with a Bengal tiger.<br /><br />The story is first introduced to the writer by a friend of the family called Mamaji and tells the writer that Pi's story will \\"make him believe in God.\\" Mamaji is a champion swimmer and there's at least one really spectacular sequence at the beginning of the film where you see Mamaji swimming. The film is shot beautifully and makes full use of eye catching perspectives including overhead shots of the ocean. Pi begins on the lifeboat with a zebra, a hyena, and an orangutan, but the animals are an intricate part of the story. It's not entirely seamless as you can tell when real animals are being used and when CG enters the picture, but the transition from one to the other is relatively flawless.<br /><br />The adventure film offers a rather marvelous message about religion as Pi discusses the experimentation with several different religions as a young boy. Even though it seems kind of silly that a boy has adopted so many religions at one point in his life, it portrays a religious message in a light that doesn't seem too preachy which is very welcome and unusual for a message of this caliber. But the religious aspect is really only a backdrop for being on your own path to finding who you really are. Feeling so alone for so long and having Pi talk about not being alone and not getting to say goodbye to those he cared about most is one of those things that just hits you really hard.<br /><br />While witnessing Pi attempt to tame Richard Parker is really entertaining, there are so many unbelievable sights to witness in \\"Life of Pi.\\" There's the whale, the jellyfish, the flying fish, that disastrous storm, and that seaweed island with all of the meerkats. \\"Life of Pi\\" never really lets up on being visually astounding from beginning to end. A personal favorite is when Pi starts seeing visions in the ocean and what he questions as being a daydream or a night dream.<br /><br />\\"Life of Pi\\" is pleasantly satisfying. With a heartfelt message, beautiful visuals, and stunning camera work, \\"Life of Pi\\" is truly a sight to behold and illustrates how essential 3D can be to a film that isn't a summer blockbuster.s full use of eye catching perspectives including overhead shots of the ocean. 0525953728|5.0|As the full title reveals this is a firsthand account of a Navy SEAL who witnessed the death of Osama Bin Laden. It is also an autobiography of his life and career up to that point.<br /><br />Mr. Owen does not sugar-coat the truth nor does he leave out the language that often accompanies that of a military member. If you are expecting a book that tells more than what is already publicly known... forget about it.<br /><br />I think the book is really well written. In particular, the Prologue is just a taste of the action before the reader sees what lead up to the infamous day. Mr. Owen intersperses personal thoughts among the action in just the right amount. 1401322786|2.0|The Time Keeper by Mitch Albom is one of those inspirational books that explicitly states its main idea within the first few pages--and then restates it again and again and again.  By the time you reach the middle of the book, you feel like shouting, \\"I get it!  Time is precious and we must appreciate it!\\"  It's not that this is a bad idea, but it would have been more interesting to have to discover it through the story instead of being constantly reminded of it.<br /><br /> I was dismayed by the anti-science slant in this novel.  The time keeper is Dor, a man from ancient times who is being punished for having discovered how to measure time.  That's right, his \\"sin\\" involved acting on his curiosity about time by studying it until he was able to understand it better; in the process, he was able to find ways to measure it.  When asked why he has done such a thing, he shamefully answers, \\"To know\\".  Knowledge is never bad!  What you do with your knowledge might be bad (and certainly some of the characters were not using their time well), but the knowledge is not to blame!<br /><br /> The book is full of errors in logic which I found irritating, the most important of which is the central idea of the novel:  the measurement of time leads to people trying to pack more activities into their lives (Why would that be?), which leads to people failing to appreciate their relationships, etc. , etc.  Oh, and electronics are bad.  We look at screens too much.  And eventually, we won't have feelings at all!  All of this is supposed to follow seamlessly, and is never questioned.<br /><br /> The novel does have some good points.  I found the character of Sarah realistic, and her difficulties were moving.  Perhaps being a former high school nerd myself helped me to understand the ways she fooled herself into believing track-star Ethan genuinely cared for her; her heartbreak when she found out differently was totally believable.  I found her story interesting, much more so than thoseof the other two main characters.<br /><br /> If you would like to read a feel-good novel which doesn't require you to do any deep thinking on your own, read The Time Keeper.  Or save yourself the trouble and read this a few times:  Don't worry about what time it is!  Use your time well!  There, you've got it!

The descriptions of the settings, buildings and scenery are so descriptive that you feel like you can actually smell the smells and feel the textures of the land.<br /><br />With so many story lines running simultaneously alongside one another the book could be seen as being overcrowded and confusing, but somehow Martin manages to give them all enough time to be understood and followed whilst seamlessly linking them together. In a book with no 'Main Character' Martin provides us with a vast selection of Heroes, Heroines and Villains that often toe the line of good and evil. You will find yourself questioning each character and wondering if the person you have trusted throughout the novel is in fact a good person. All the characters are flawed and no-one is truly good or bad, each have their own goal and their own motives which add to the depth of the story.<br /><br />I would recommend this book to everyone, and if like me you have watched the HBO Series, then I cannot stress enough that you read the book as well. It contains little details and characters that could not be included in the Show but make the story so much more than it is on TV.<br /><br />I am now racing to finish the whole set as the story has me completely gripped!

0140177396|5.0|\\"Of Mice and Men\\" features two migrant farm workers during the Great Depression in California.<br /><br />The book is about dreams. George and Lennie just want a piece of land to call their own, and they believe in this dream strongly enough that other characters start to buy in too. A place for soft things; a place for independence; a place for respect; a place to live in peace. This is tied in very strongly to socioeconomic status, age, and race, and the issues that it brings up about the American dream are as relevant today as they were then.<br /><br />The language was interesting. It is apparent that the novel was written many decades ago, and there are a bunch of turns of phrase that I had never heard before (but could guess at, for the most part).<br /><br />I liked the structure. One character was disagreeable and one character was mean, but there wasn't really an antagonist. It really was a good description of the best laid plans of mice and men going awry. I like this style because a lot of the injustices that happen today aren't the result of one villain's wrongdoing, but rather a system that makes people poor and hungry and where people don't understand one another. For a short book, Steinbeck does a very good job of creating empathy with the different characters such that the reader can understand their wrongdoing and still appreciate them as a person.<br /><br />Something that I learned: in the US, you can't execute mentally handicapped citizens for their crimes, but the Supreme Court left it up to states that practice the death penalty how to interpret that. Apparently, Texas' standard is that someone is exempt from the death penalty if they are as intelligent as Lennie Small [...]. Horrifying.

The band has shown outstanding experimentation in stylistical crossovers, innovative soundscapes, performance techniques, and metaphor- and humor-packed storytelling during the first half of the 1970s. \\"A Trick of the Tail\\" was release in 1976, a year after flamboyant lead singer Peter Gabriel had left the band, and roughly a year before guitarist Steve Hackett would also leave the band. This critically acclaimed album came to life through a mist of widespread skepticism about the fate of the band, and could be considered as an apex of the whole prog rock phase. The next album (Wind & wuthering) would mark its end, showing that the band was beginning to steer in a more pop-oriented direction.<br />So in my opinion Genesis' purely prog rock phase culminates in \\"A Trick of the Tail\\", which makes it so special. In this album, the musicianship displayed by Banks, Rutherford, Hackett and Collins is absolutely amazing. It is no exaggeration to say that \\"Ripples\\" is one of the band's deepest songs at so many levels, and \\"Los Endos\\" is epically defining a whole musical era. \\"Dance on a Volcano\\" and \\"Squonk\\" are genuine explosions of musical energy.<br />If you are approaching Genesis for the first time, this is probably where I would advise you start. B0087ZG7HK|5.0|Jurassic Park is a science fiction movie based on the novel of the same name by Michael Crichton. It is a story about how as much as man tries to be in control of everything, life will find a way around the boundaries we try to confine it to. Jurassic Park stars Sam Neill, Laura Dern, Jeff Goldblum, and Richard Attenborough.<br /><br />An incident at a biological preserve on an island off the coast of Costa Rica has prompted a review of the resort by the investors. John Hammond (Attenborough), CEO of InGen, has invited several consultants as guests for a weekend to determine the safety of the park. They include paleontologist Dr. Alan Grant (Neill), paleobotanist Ellie Sattler (Dern), and mathematician Ian Malcolm (Goldblum). The guests are stunned to discover that the park is the home of genetically engineered dinosaurs. Hammond's grandchildren arrive to join the adults on the tour of the park. However, as a storm approaches the island, an espionage scheme is afoot to steal dinosaur embryos that results in the total failure of the security system. Its up to Dr. Grant to get Hammond's grandchildren, Lex (Ariana Richards) and Tim (Joseph Mazzello).<br /><br />Jurassic Park was an awe inspiring visual effects masterpiece when released in 1993. At that time, very few movies had computer generated characters that interacted with live actors, and none of them at that time had the level of realism seem in the dinosaurs in Jurassic Park. Compared to a lot of other action movies from the 1990s that relied heavily on CG effects, Jurassic Park's effects still stand up fairly well. I am interested in seeing how well it has been cleaned up for the 3-D release next year.<br /><br />Jurassic Park is rated PG-13 for intense science fiction terror. This movie requires a personal judgement call on whether its suitable for young children to watch. There is only a very small amount of strong language, most of which can be attributed to a then relatively unknown Samuel L. Jackson. The main scenes that you may not want your small children to see are the ones where people are killed by dinosaurs, although there are only one or two death scenes that are truly gruesome, as most of them leave the blood shed to the imagination. B0041KVW2K|3.0|I had always suspected that EMI's reluctance to again offer The Beatles albums on vinyl was because, since neither EMI nor Capitol have had their own vinyl factory for more than 20 years, that they(EMI) & Capitol) would be at the mercy of outside pressing plants, and that EMI & Capitol would have absolutely no control over quality. And this is exactly what happened. And EMI & Capitol didn't help things by selecting a pressing plant(for the U.S.A. release) that has a notorious reputation for off-center grooves, off-center labels & noisy surfaces.<br /><br />  I purchased from a popular New York City internet dealer, \\"J&R Music World\\"(albeit through Amazon Payments). The dealer packed the set well with bubble paper. I was luckier than most people. 13 of the 16 records in my set ranged from passable to very good, but the remaining three were horrible, and fortunately the dealer was willing to exchange individual L.P.'s so I wouldn't have to send back the entire box set. Hopefully, the replacement records will arrive soon, and they'll be of acceptable quality.<br /><br />  Of the 3 records that I had to return, \\"Abbey Road\\" was very crackly, and run out groove area was a storm of noise(it looked as if the stampers had been rubbed down with sandpaper at the pressing plant). \\"Rubber Soul\\" had an off-center label on \\"Side One\\", and a repetitive scratch through two-thirds of the song \\"Girl\\". And \\"Sgt.Pepper's Lonely Hearts Club Band\\" had \\"Side Two\\" grooves that were 1/8th of an inch off-center....and therefore audible towards the end of the side. I am realistic: there is little chance of getting a U.S.A. manufactured 2012 \\"Abbey Road\\" L.P. that will play properly.<br /><br />  I test for off-center grooves by starting to play the first song on a side. i then close the dust cover lid on my(Technics SL1210Mk.2) turntable, then I hold my finger on the dustcover lid, directly over the tonearm's headshell, and I look to see if the headshell is moving to and fro.<br /><br />  4 other records had off-center grooves on \\"side two\\". For 3 of those, the grooves were 1/32nd of an inch off-center, and so not audible, and for one record(side two of \\"Magical Mystery Tour\\") 1/16th of an inch off-center. Fortunately, that side has only 5 songs, and the grooves don't come close to the label area, so playback is acceptable.<br /><br />  And tonight I noticed a defect in my book. The pages are originally printed larger than their intended size, then the excess paper is trimmed off before binding . But one page(Pages 59/60, which includes part of  the \\"Beatles For Sale\\" front cover photo outtake) was seriously folded before trimming. Unfolding the page left a permanently creased and cracked page, and I had to use a scissors to trim off the excess paper flap that was supposed to be trimmed off before binding.<br /><br />  The Beatles are EMI's flagship group, and their music deserved the finest possible manufacturing and quality control. Rainbo Records(the pressing plant that manufactured the records) should put things right for the consumer, but from a standpoint of their manufacturing capabilities, they aren't competent to put things right. In the End, it is the names of EMI & Apple Records that went onto the product, so they should put things right. It is essential that these companies have the trust of Beatles fans, particularly with another Beatles vinyl box(the mono L.P.'s) over the horizon within the next 5 months.<br /><br />  The ball is in EMI & Capitol's court now. The shoddy quality control during pressing is really sad, because much effort went into mastering the music at Abbey Road Studios. The overall sound of the remasters is excellent, though different from previous vinyl editions.<br /><br />UPDATE: On November 20,2012, I sent the 3 defective records back to the dealer in New York City. Unfortunately(3 times) a postal sort facility  in New Jersey mistakenly sent my package to Denver,Colorado so it took 3 weeks for my package to arrive atthe dealer. The dealer didn't acknowledge receiving the package until a week after they received it, then they waited another week before sending replacement records, which arrived December 27,2012. This time,\\"Sgt.Pepper\\" plays outstanding with dead quiet surfaces. \\"Rubber Soul\\" also has quiet surfaces, though with very slightly off-center grooves on \\"Side Two\\", but not enough to be audible. As for \\"Abbey Road\\", I still didn't get a fully satisfactory copy, though it is much better than my first copy.  \\"Side One\\" is fine, but \\"Side Two\\" has a visible(and to varying extents audible) scratch through one-third of \\"Here Comes The Sun\\". The remainder of the side plays passably, but not as quiet as it should have.While not warped at the edge, I can see my phono cartridge going up and down, so there's a warp inward. But, unfortunately, though the dealer packed the 3 replacement L.p.'s in a big box with lots of bubble paper, at some point, someone grabbed the three album covers by the corner(not realizing that these album covers are made from thinner cardboard than in the good ol' days) and irreparably creased the corner(from the lower right corner inwards 1.5 inches) of all three album covers, and it is particularly visible on the rear of the album covers, and the inside of the \\"Sgt.Peppers\\" gatefold cover. It seems that I just can't win. This mirrors my experience getting replacement CD's for the two incorrectly mastered discs in \\"The Capitol albums Vol.2\\" CD box set. At first, Capitol said \\"send back the discs and sleeves\\", then shortly after I sent my discs back, they said, \\"send back the discs only\\"...and of course, when I received my replacement \\"Rubber Soul\\" & \\"Beatles VI\\" CD's, the sleeves were badly creased, because Capitol simply put them into an envelope with no protective material.<br /><br />  Eventually, probably the next time that I order something from Amazon's British company, I'll order a European-manufactured \\"Abbey Road\\" L.P., and hopefully then have a complete box set with all the records in good condition. I'll still have damaged album covers for \\"Sgt.Peppers\\" & \\"Rubber Soul\\", and the factory defect in my book. I am becoming more and more wary of EMI's forthcoming mono vinyl box set. Those records will probably not be offered separately outside of the box set, and unless Capitol & EMI have some system in place for consumers to exchange defective records so consumers can \\"Build\\" a perfect set....I'll have to pass. I already have the 1982 Japanese red vinyl mono L.P. series, and(excepting the phasey, flawed mastering of the title track on \\"A Hard Days Night\\") those Japanese L.P.'s sound fantastic.<br /><br />UPDATE(Jan.23,2013): I eventually did buy a European-manufactured \\"Abbey Road\\" L.P. from Amazon.co.uk, and what people are saying about the European pressings is true: they are of superior quality, with better sound quality,lower surface noise, and better(overall) appearance. But, once again, I got a badly creased sleeve. As it stands now, I have a complete box set with all records playing from passable to excellent, but with three damaged album covers(Sgt.Peppers, Rubber Soul & Abbey Road) and a slightly defective book.  Shortly after I ordered a European \\"Abbey Road\\" L.P.(buying the album again after two U.S.A. copies were bad), I got Capitol's e-mail address and sent them an e-mail about the problems I have experienced. They e-mailed back saying that I would receive some replacement records in 2 to 4 weeks.<br /><br />UPDATE(Jan.25,2013): 23 days after Capitol responded to my e-mail, I received a package(by UPS) from Rainbo Records. Capitol hadn't really entirely understood my e-mail. I needed the \\"Abbey Road\\" record and album cover & album covers-only for \\"Rubber Soul\\" & \\"Sgt.Pepper's\\". Rainbo sent records-only(in generic white album covers) for those 3 albums. And how were these 3 records? \\"Abbey Road\\" was the most satisfactory of the 3 U.S.A.-pressings I've had. Quiet surfaces,slightly warped(but playable), slightly off-center grooves on \\"side one\\"(but not enough to be audible) and an unevenly trimmed edge. \\"Rubber Soul\\" was not unlike the 2nd copy that I have: slightly off-center grooves on \\"side two\\"(but not enough to be audible), but the overall fidelity was superior to the second copy. \\"Sgt.Pepper's\\" was fine; very nearly equal in quality to the second copy that I got.<br /><br />But none of this resolves the problem of the damaged album covers that I got with the replacement L.P's from the New York City dealer. This is the end of my struggles with this box set. I'm not making any further attempts. As for buying 3 of these albums again for the album covers, it would be too risky to do that via mail order. Go to a local record store(where I could inspect the album covers before buying) you might ask? If there only WAS a local record store, I would. As for EMI's forthcoming box set of the mono L.P.'s, if I buy it, it will be the European edition. Rainbo (the U.S.A. pressing plant) can't reliably align the two stampers when installing them onto their record pressing machines.<br /><br />As for the box set with the various upgrades(replacement L.P.'s) that I installed, what I now have is fine for everyday, general purpose listening. Audiophile product? No. Collectors item? The three damaged album covers ensure that it will never be a collectors-grade item. It's a bummer that I've had to put in two months of hassles and waiting trying to build a defect-free set, and this has all been (as the British say) \\"For Naught\\".<br /><br />With this box set, released almost exactly 50 years after EMI started to market Beatles music, the company had come full circle, back to where the marketing of Beatles music began......with vinyl records. Too bad that after all these years, that this box set was a bungled, botched farewell from EMI to The Beatles fans. EMI is now being dismantled, and it is now apparent that Universal Music(who bought EMI) is now having second thoughts and seeking to recoup the enormous purchase price. Universal is now going to sell off much more of EMI than the European & American regulators require, and that ultimately, the only parts of EMI that Universal wants to keep are The Beatles catalog, Capitol Records(and its subsidiary labels) and the \\"Virgin\\" label. Almost all of EMI's non-Beatles UK back catalog is now(as I type this) up for bidding....to, essentially, be auctioned off. This is really a sad day for music fans.<br /><br />UPDATE 2014: I bought \\"Abbey Road\\" & \\"SGt.Peppers\\" AGAIN(from an Amazon \\"Marketplace\\" merchant, \\"Ernie B's Reggae\\") just to get album covers in good condition. And the album covers were in good condition. And how were the pressing? \\"Sgt.Peppers\\" was the best sounding pressing yet, but with the label attached off-center on \\"Side 2\\". \\"Abbey Road\\" was unsatisfactory, with a repetitive scratch through the last 50 seconds of the album. I combined my best(so far) pressing of \\"Abbey Road\\"(the European pressing that I bought from Amazon.co.uk) with the new album cover from Ernie B's, and I combined the \\"Sgt.Peppers\\" replacement record from \\"J&R\\" with the new album cover from Ernie B.'s.<br /><br />Then, due to the off-center grooves on \\"Side 2\\" of my U.S.A.-pressed \\"Help\\" and all three U.S.A. copies of \\"Rubber Soul\\" that I tried, I ordered the European pressings from a Uk dealer \\"Spin CD's\\". Both were superb pressings, but both arrived with damaged album covers. I installed these European records into my U.S.A. album covers. Also, tired of the \\"non-fill scraping noises on \\"Side 1\\" of my U.S.A.pressing of \\"Let It Be\\", I bought a UK \\"Let it Be\\" album from amazon.co.uk. The pressing and album cover were acceptable. I also TRIED to buy a European \\"Please Please Me\\" L.P. from an Amazon.co.uk \\"Marketplace\\" merchant, but the merchant was dishonest, and they supplied the U.S.A. pressing(Amazon.co.uk refunded me, and let me keep the L.P.). This L.P. was a quiet pressing, but with a very slight warp, whichhad no effect on play.<br /><br />And, where does this leave me today?(July 2014). I have all of the album covers in good condition(except a slightly creased \\"Rubber Soul\\" album cover), and the records are as follows:<br />Please Please Me(U.S.A. pressing. Generally fine, with slight warp)<br />With The Beatles(U.S.A. pressing. Slightly off-center grooves on \\"Side 2\\", but not enough to be audible.)<br />A Hard Days Night(U.S.A. pressing. 159420411X|4.0|I'm not the kind of person who loves every book of this style. I generally think that Malcolm Gladwell and Thomas Friedman just find cute ways to repeat things other people have already said. But I thought this book was completely different. Instead of finding cute new phrases to repeat old information, Nate Silver finds clear and concise ways to convey interesting, new information. I know that none of the mathematics he's conveying is new, but he does an insightful job of explaining how thinking in a Bayesian way can help in forecasting all sorts of world events and how actual outcomes can be used to improve our understanding of how the world works. Despite his non-academic background Nate Silver has made significant contributions to political forecasting. His forecasts are arguably better than and certainly on par with Princeton Professor (admittedly, not a professor of social sciences, so his professor job may not be very relevant to this conversation) Sam Wang. It's not just that Silver's numbers get closer to reality, but that he has a comprehensive approach that uses all information, appropriately weighted and with a wary eye towards overconfidence.<br /><br />Sometimes, I will say, that writing is a little grating (\\"...a stat head's wet dream!\\" - awkward). The chapter on baseball forecasting is pretty confusing if you don't already know a ton about baseball (I don't). And the chapter on Hurricane forecasting seems to miss the mark pretty badly. He has interesting things to say about the numbers around hurricane forecasts, but veers off in a crazy direction when offering a political interpretation of those numbers. He never mentions levees and makes one very brief, uncritical reference to FEMA. After explaining how great hurricane forecasts are these days he basically lays the blame for what happened in New Orleans on the victims. I guess he just wasn't thinking very hard about this part of the book, and neither was his editor. But overall it's a great read!

B0072GPQNG|3.0|Spielberg has a long history as a master story-teller for both children and adults and has made many five-star movies, but in `Warhorse' seems to have lost his magic touch.<br /><br />Despite a lavish budget, spectacular set pieces and a very real-looking re-creation of the front-line horrors of the 1914-18 war, `Warhorse' is overall a cheesy and unconvincing affair with a so-so screenplay. Uncharacteristically (for Spielberg) poor editing contributes to a rather chopped-up storyline which lacks the usual powerful and engaging narrative continuity found in the films of this erstwhile great magician of the silver screen. The story is all there; it just isn't realised very well.<br /><br />The film has many positives. Spielberg's classic large-scale cinematography is at times truly breathtaking; the horses are magnificently trained & highly photogenic; the soundtrack is good; the attention to period detail exemplary - as far as this non-expert reviewer can tell.<br /><br />However the film's failings make for quite a list: poor casting, unconvincing acting, some peculiar and not-quite-right British regional accents, Germans unfortunately speaking English to each other with German accents (is the audience really judged to be so dumb that they can't read subtitles?), some beyond-believable plot devices which verge on the embarrassing, excessive sentimentality - one of Spielberg's consistent failings but usually offset by his excellent narrative storytelling - together with the poor editing and deficiencies in script make for an uninvolving viewing experience.<br /><br />The film's main failing, however, remains that it is unsure of its audience. Is it a feel-good film for kids? The war scenes are surely too bloody, violent and upsetting for small children. At the same time it's too simplistic, predictable and cheesy to succeed as a serious film for grown-ups. Either way we don't care enough about the characters - except maybe the horse. This unfortunately condemns the film as one of the director's less successful efforts, and will probably deny it `classic' status in future years. You can't help but feel that with such a generous budget and experienced film maker, a better result might have been offered.ilm as one of the director's less successful efforts, and will probably deny it `classic' status in future years. You can't help but feel that with such a generous budget and experienced film maker, a better result might have been offered.

B0031YJFCQ|5.0|I just finished reading the Millennium series (The Girl with the Dragon Tattoo (2008), The Girl Who Played With Fire (2009), The Girl Who Kicked the Hornet's Nest (2010)) last night and wanted to comment on it in this public forum...not sure what I can add to understanding of the three books...or the plot or why you should read them, but I'll give it a try. I will highly recommend this series to anyone who wants a wild, entertaining ride into the world of high-suspense crime fiction. The books excel at painting an eerie and foreboding atmosphere. There are flawed likeable characters, memorable villains (you always need them) and enough plot twists and turns to keep everyone on their toes...it is all here and it leaps out at you.<br /><br />I find it fascinating that some of the works of pop culture which I have enjoyed the most in the last year are Hanna (2011) (movie with Saoirse Ronan as a highly-trained assassin), The Hunger Games trilogy, (The Hunger Games (2007), Catching Fire (2009) and Mockingjay (2010) and Millennium series. Interesting that both second books from the Hunger Games trilogy and the Millennium series have fire in their title...Catching Fire (2009) and The Girl Who Played With Fire (2009).<br /><br />All the protagonists in these works are female, fairly young and all defend them self quite well in intellectual, emotional and physical confrontations. Perhaps, I am \\"maled-out\\" (I just made that term up) from viewing and reading about so many male protagonists that I am ready for something completely different. These female characters are fresh, young, bright and have immense appeal.<br /><br />Like many others, I found Lisbeth Salander utterly fascinating. Her diminutive size, gender, attitude and  hacking ability make her someone who I just could not get enough of. When the narrative was about others or other plot lines, I patiently waited (okay, sometimes not so patiently) for the action to go back to Salander, and when it did, my interest was once again peaked. I couldn't wait to find out what she was going to do next. She was, at times, compelling, conflicted, idiosyncratic and complicated..and sometimes she exhibited all of those qualities at one time. I have a feeling that Lisbeth will stay in my mind...and stay.<br /><br />As for this particular book (The Girl Who Kicked the Hornet's Nest (2010))...although some have stated in their review that there were too many subplots, I enjoyed the intricate details, the developing storylines and  the many characters that the book provided. That is not to say that I didn't occasionally have to go back to review exactly who a person was and what was their identity/role. I liked the character Suzanne Linder (Erika Berger's bodyguard) and appreciated a bit of her back story. Her character was well drawn out and added to the enjoyment of the book. The online chat with Berger and Salander was intriguing as you felt that each found the exchange a bit uncomfortable, but both seemed to realize that they needed each other. The ongoing dynamic of Berger's new job and her stalker added more suspense, but you always knew that she would end up back at Millennium. And I also loved Dr. Teleborian getting in the end...that bastard had it coming. Who carries their \\"dirty\\" laptop into in a courtroom and gets arrested?.....an arrogant, corrupt pervert, that's who. It was all neatly wrapped up by Stieg Larsson and it all made sense.<br /><br />One of the highlights of the book for me was when Lisbeth entered the courtroom wearing a shirt that said \\"I am Annoyed\\"....did anyone else pick that up?. Honestly, I had to put the book down while I burst out laughing. It all made perfect sense to me.....this girl coming into court with her life on the line, wearing a shirt that basically says...\\"this is a joke, you are a joke and I am put out to even be here\\". Who knew a moment of high drama could contain such humorous irony?<br /><br />I so enjoyed reading this series and stopped at intervals to savor it as the book (and the series) came to a conclusion.....knowing that there would be no more from this author. But, alas, there is a strong indication that Larsson's live-in girlfriend has a fourth story in her possession. Larsson's father and brother have stated in an interview that they saw it, so you never know. Imagine the excitement that a fourth book would create! What would happen next? Perhaps the developing saga of Lisbeth's twin sister Camilla. Is she in trouble or has she too been take advantage in the past? Or could there be another Zalachenko offspring hiding out somewhere with orders to eliminate Lisbeth in the event of Papa Zalachenko's death? What will Lisbeth do with all of her money? What happens to the relationship between Lisbeth and Blomkvist? Does Lisbeth, with the knowledge that so many helped her, change in any way? Is there another tale of Swedish corruption at the highest level of government, business, banking or personal security? 0812992784|4.0|This is a wonderful history of the author's experiences after being targeted by a fatwa from the Ayatollah Khomeini. It picks up the story at the very beginning of the rise of state sponsored terrorism and stakes out the battle ground between western secular free speech and the Islamic fundamentalism that has come to dominate so much of our world history. The book is filled with quotable snippets of wisdom. My copy is marred with yellow highlighter.  Unfortunately, the author seems hell bent on mentioning every literary celebrity he even spent five minutes with. For me it undermined his courage and determination to continue his literary career under the often oppressive eye of British protective services. The name dropping reaches often absurd proportions, which only raises the role of oversized egos in all of this. Still it is a well written and page turning read. And it outlines the ongoing debate of the free speech vs. this extreme form of censorship, while maintaining sensitivity to the diverse populations, some of whom are more than willing to kill to remain in their cultural bubble.Reads like a thoughful spy thriller for the most part.

0316228532|4.0|There are two camps when it comes to The Casual Vacancy. The first camp finds the book slow and very dull. These people might be the ones that are angry that this book isn't related to the world of Harry Potter. The second camp love the book and find it fascinating. These might be the people that will read anything that J.K. Rowling writes just because she's J.K. Rowling.<br /><br />I don't belong to either of these camps, but I loved the book anyway. First of all, as a general warning, this book is character-driven, not plot-driven. There are a lot of characters that are introduced, but I didn't find it hard to keep track of them. In the story, nothing really happens. The characters all just react to the death and the book describes the complexity of life while a community is coping with loss. It's a bleak book. Everything is tinted with a feeling of hopelessness and depression and most people are unhappy. Basically, Rowling wrote about life in small-town England and she made no apologies for how honest it is. There are elements of casual sex, rape, drug use, and self-harm in this book and copious amounts of swearing to go along with it. It's by no means pretty, but it's resounding in its sincerity.<br /><br />To sum up, if you like to read books as an escape from everyday life, this book may not be for you. It's not light-hearted, it won't make you smile. However, if you like a dose of reality in your books and you're interested in the complexities of people, then pick it up. Rowling proves she's an incredible writer and her career as an author isn't over just because Harry Potter is.

B009AMANBA|5.0|This superb motion picture focuses on the intense political maneuvering and bargaining during January 1865 that led to the passage of the Thirteenth Amendment in the House of Representatives.  While many of us may have considered the Emancipation Proclamation (published after the Union victory at Antietam in September 1862 and effective on January 1, 1863) to be the event that \\"freed the slaves\\" and for which Abraham Lincoln has been considered our greatest president, the actual outlawing of Slavery throughout the United States did not come until the 13th Amendment to the Constitution was passed in both houses of Congress and formally ratified by the States at the end of 1865.  The legal necessity for this Amendment is carefully and clearly explained during this movie and gives gravity to this immensely important legislative activity.<br /><br />This is not a sweeping biographical study of Lincoln nor even the depiction of his entire presidency as was the dramatization of Gore Vidal's LINCOLN (1988) so ably performed by Sam Waterson and Mary Tyler Moore.  It is, rather, an intense focus on one set of events near the end of Lincoln's life and presidency that captures with greater clarity and precision the essential greatness of the man and enormous implications of the political debates facing the Congress at the time.<br /><br />Daniel Day Lewis gives what is certainly the single best interpretation of Lincoln I have ever seen, but the supporting cast is also extremely effective.  Tommy Lee Jones (as Congressman Thaddeus Stevens), Bruce McGill (as the irritable and blustery Secretary of War Stanton) and Sally Field (the acute, but deeply disturbed Mary Todd Lincoln), all render memorable performances.  The human toll of war are also presented without resorting to such faux battle re-enactments as were presented in the 1988 TV movie.  Wagons of severed limbs and mangled bodies portray the carnage in this film without resorting to inadequate action sequences.<br /><br />This will undoubtedly be a prime Oscar contender for 2012 and probably be numbered among the great motion pictures of all time./>This will undoubtedly be a prime Oscar contender for 2012 and probably be numbered among the great motion pictures of all time.

0316187216|5.0|Red Country is Abercrombie's third stand-alone novel set in the same world as his First Law trilogy.  While reading the prior books is not necessary to follow the story, I think it really enhances the experience, as there are many plot points and characters that are easier to understand if you know the backstory.<br /><br />The book revolves are Shy South, a woman with a troubled past who is trying to keep the family farm running.  When the farm is burned and her brother and sister are kidnapped she vows to track down the attackers and get her siblings back.  In order to do so she will need to chase them across the Far Country, an unsettled, brutal land in the midst of a gold rush.  Her father-in-law Lamb, who she believes to be the biggest coward alive, accompanies her due to a promise he made to her mother.<br /><br />The story sounds simple, but as it continues it keeps adding more and more to the mix.  Along the way they find interesting characters to accompany them, join up with a group of settlers heading towards the rumors of gold, get embroiled in the battle for the town where the gold rush is centered, and finally get sucked into the politics of the brewing war between the Union and the Old Empire.  Some familiar faces from previous books play a role, Cosca, Friendly, and Caul Shivers just to name a few.  Consistent with the previous books there are really no cut and dry good guys, it's a dark and dirty world and even the \\"heroes\\" aren't going to come out clean.<br /><br />The highlight for me is Lamb.  I won't spoil who he is, but if you've read any of the previous books you probably already know.  If this series is Abercrombie's take on a western movie, the Lamb is Clint Eastwood's character from The Unforgiven (which I would swear there are some lines from in the book, not the same, but close enough that it made me wonder if it was intentional..... or I could just be reading too much into it).  Lamb is the killer who has tried to put the violent past behind him and start fresh, slowly getting dragged back into the old life.  This has always been among my favorite characters in the series, and it's a welcome return, even if the character might wish differently.<br /><br />In conclusion, simply stated, this is my favorite fantasy novel I've read this year, best I've read since the previous book in the series.  It manages to tell a great story on its own while continuing to develop the storylines in Abercrombie's world.  Highly recommended!

This case had always troubled Bosch and he gladly accepts the challenge although after all that time the trail has gone cold.<br /><br />Bosch is an impatient detective - to him momentum is everything. Once he is on the trail he is a bloodhound who never lets up until he finds a break. He calls this \\"The Black Box\\" because, similar to air crash investigation a single verified clue may open up the whole case. After diligent and clever police work Bosch finds his Black Box and discovers a web of intrigue and violence going back to the first Gulf War.<br /><br />Working the case in his normal independent manner is not helped by his a strained relationship with and lack of respect for the competence of his superiors at LAPD, especially his current Lieutenant (O'Toole - nickname \\"O'Fool\\").  \\"You are the worst kind of police officer, Bosch. You are arrogant, a bully, and you think the laws and regulations don't apply to you.\\" O'Toole refers Bosch to Internal Affairs on what seems to be a petty matter, but it is important because it affects the way Bosch can run the investigation and if the complaint is upheld he could easily lose his job because he is on a DROP contract.<br /><br />Connelly keeps up the pressure and spins an exciting tale of skilled police investigation by a dedicated, independent but somewhat personally flawed Harry Bosch. I recommend this book as a great read for lovers of police procedurals and a good Christmas present for those who still read print books.by a dedicated, independent but somewhat personally flawed Harry Bosch. B0041KVW2K|1.0|Analog happens only once. Original sounds are emitted and recorded onto open reel magnetic tape. (40+ years ago that is!). \\"Vinyl\\" was cut from those master Beatles tapes and vinyl maintained the analog chain quite nicely right into your home.  Short of listening to the original master and that aint happenin'... the best quality is the Vinyl cut from the master tape ie, what they did originally. It is still PURE 100% Analog. Then this debauchery came along. IF one is to convert the master tapes to a digital format then it's digital from that point forward. It has lost it's analog component forever and ever. Information is missing and that has been accepted fact for some time. There is NO returning to analog once a signal has been digitized. It doesn't work that way. The conversion only goes in one direction. analog ----> to digital. There is NO Reverse. People who DO reverse it as in this case, make a fraud of the whole affair and mislead people into thinking because it's vinyl spinning around its analog or at least somehow closer to analog. No it's not! This method can't be taken seriously so one must conclude its a marketing deception. Add to that the poor pressing history and it's quite a failure sonically. No amount of EQ dynamic restoration , limiting, compression, etc, can bring missing information back. If you wanted true analog, where will you find it? I dunno, but not here. Keep searching.

0765350386|5.0|The Mistborn novel is truly an original, stand out piece of Fantasy, in that it not only focuses on Sanderson's new type of magic, but the tense plot to over throw a tyrannical ruler. Sanderson pieces together a crew of thieves and vagabonds to form a close knit group of men that fight together for the freedom of a subjugated race of men and women.  Leading this group is a common stereotype seen in many fantasy novels but never utilized as Sanderson has wonderfully done here. Kelsier is a thief with an odd set of morals, willing to fight and destroy the Lord Ruler, a self-appointed god over all men. A Mistborn himself, Kelsier wields the power of Allomancy, using metals to fuel various types of powers.<br /><br />The story, however, focuses on Vin, a street rat who is discovered by Kelsier to be a Mistborn like himself. Through training and well written sparring scenes, Sanderson's wholly original magic is downright believable and truly unlike anything fantasy readers have witnessed so far. Joining this group of thieves willing to overthrow the Final Empire, Vin grows drastically into a powerful Mistborn determined to fight alongside Kelsier in his quest. The novel takes off into a world of intrigue and realism, constantly bringing in new magical elements that keep the reader glued to the pages. Many questions are raised, some answered, and some left to the following novels. The novel lays a wonderful foundation for what lies ahead, incorporating fantasy, action, and Sanderson's clean writing fashion into an original work of art.
